update OPS$ORACLE.PRODUCTION_FOCUS_EXCEPTIONS set END_DATE=sysdate+15 where STATUS='DBAOPS-97045';

select * from OPS$ORACLE.PRODUCTION_FOCUS_EXCEPTIONS where STATUS='DBAOPS-97045';

select a.tbl "Name",a.tsz "Total Size",b.fsz "Free Space", round((1-(b.fsz/a.tsz))*100) "Pct Used",
round((b.fsz/a.tsz)*100) "Pct Free" from (select tablespace_name tbl,sum(bytes)/1024/1024 TSZ from dba_data_files 
where tablespace_name like '%UNDO%' group by tablespace_name) a, (select tablespace_name tblsp,sum(bytes)/1024/1024 FSZ 
from dba_free_space where tablespace_name like '%SYSTEM%' group by tablespace_name) b Where a.tbl=b.tblsp;

set lines 400
set pages 999
col GROUP_NAME for a35
SELECT
name group_name
, sector_size sector_size
, block_size block_size
, allocation_unit_size allocation_unit_size
, state state
, type type
, round(total_mb/1024,2) total_gb
, round((total_mb - free_mb)/1024,2) used_gb
,round(free_mb/1024,2) free_gb
, ROUND((1- (free_mb / total_mb))*100, 2) pct_used
FROM
v$asm_diskgroup
ORDER BY
name
;

 CHECK INSTANCE STATUS

set lines 200 pages 200
COL HOST_NAME FOR A30
COL FORCE_LOGGING FOR A15
COL DB_UNIQUE_NAME FOR A20

ALTER SESSION SET NLS_DATE_FORMAT = 'DD.MM.YYYY HH24:MI:SS';
SELECT INST_ID,INSTANCE_NAME,HOST_NAME,STATUS,LOGINS,STARTUP_TIME,DATABASE_STATUS FROM GV$INSTANCE ORDER BY INST_ID;
SELECT INST_ID,NAME,OPEN_MODE,DATABASE_ROLE,LOG_MODE,FLASHBACK_ON,DB_UNIQUE_NAME,FORCE_LOGGING FROM GV$DATABASE ORDER BY INST_ID;
select inst_id,name,open_mode,OPEN_TIME from gv$pdbs;

MRP Status :
===========
set lines 400
select inst_id,process,client_process,status,thread#,sequence#,block#,blocks from gv$managed_standby where PROCESS like '%MRP%'; 

select arch.thread# "Thread",arch.sequence# "Last Sequence Received", appl.sequence# "Last Sequence Applied",(arch.sequence# - appl.sequence#) "Difference"
from
(select thread#,max(sequence#) as sequence#  from v$archived_log  where RESETLOGS_CHANGE# = (SELECT RESETLOGS_CHANGE# FROM V$DATABASE_INCARNATION  WHERE STATUS = 'CURRENT')
and archived = 'YES' group by thread# order by thread#)arch,
(select thread#,max(sequence#) as sequence# from v$archived_log   where RESETLOGS_CHANGE# = (SELECT RESETLOGS_CHANGE# FROM V$DATABASE_INCARNATION  WHERE STATUS = 'CURRENT')
and applied = 'YES' group by thread# order by thread#) appl
where arch.thread# = appl.thread#;

(

and REQUEST_TIME < SYSDATE-20/(24*60) 
order by 1;
);

set lines 400

col GROUP_NAME for a35
SELECT
name group_name
, sector_size sector_size
, block_size block_size
, allocation_unit_size allocation_unit_size
, state state
, type type
, round(total_mb/1024,2) total_gb
, round((total_mb - free_mb)/1024,2) used_gb
,round(free_mb/1024,2) free_gb
--, ROUND((1- (free_mb / total_mb))*100, 2) pct_used
FROM
v$asm_diskgroup
ORDER BY
name
;

Primary Lost Write Option 1: Determine if affected objects can be recreated and recovery allowed to continue:

1. First determine the affected objects. The alert log message will provide the datafile number along with the corresponding block number. For blocks containing user data, the alert log may also report the data object number. Using this information you can determine which objects are affected by the corruption:

Spool the output and keep them handy.
SQL> Select * from DBA_EXTENTS
     where FILE_ID=&file_number and
     &block_number BETWEEN BLOCK_ID and BLOCK_ID+BLOCKS-1;

If the error provides the object number determine the affected object with the following query:

SQL> Select * from DBA_OBJECTS    where DATA_OBJECT_ID = &object_number;

2. If feasible, drop and recreate the affected objects on the primary.

3. Once the objects have been recreated, use the following procedure to skip corrupted block on the standby:

Temporarily disable lost write protection on the standby:
SQL> ALTER SYSTEM SET DB_LOST_WRITE_PROTECT = NONE; 

Allow recovery to proceed in spite of block corruptions by running the RECOVER command with the ALLOW n CORRUPTION clause, where n is the number of allowable corrupt blocks.
SQL> alter database recover automatic standby database
     allow 1 corruption;

Once the alert log indicates the blocks have been marked corrupt, restart managed recovery.
SQL> alter database recover cancel;
SQL> alter database recover managed standby database using current logfile disconnect;
 
Re-enable lost write protection on the standby so future lost writes can be detected:
SQL> ALTER SYSTEM SET DB_LOST_WRITE_PROTECT = TYPICAL;

select
"Reserved_Space(GB)", "Reserved_Space(GB)" - "Free_Space(GB)" "Used_Space(GB)",
"Free_Space(GB)"
from(
select 
(select sum(bytes/(1024*1024*1024)) from v$datafile) "Reserved_Space(GB)",
(select sum(bytes/(1024*1024*1024)) from dba_free_space) "Free_Space(GB)"
from dual
);

 SELECT DISTINCT fcp.user_concurrent_program_name,
                fcp.concurrent_program_name,
                fcr.request_id,
                fcr.request_date,
                flv.meaning status,
                fcr.status_code,
                fcr.logfile_name,
                fcr.outfile_name,
                fcr.argument_text "Program Parameters",
                 fcr.completion_text,
                 TO_CHAR(fcr.request_date, 'DD-MON-YYYY HH24:MI:SS') requested
     , TO_CHAR(fcr.requested_start_date, 'DD-MON-YYYY HH24:MI:SS') requested_start  
     , TO_CHAR((fcr.requested_start_date), 'HH24:MI:SS') start_time
  FROM apps.fnd_concurrent_programs_vl fcp,
       apps.fnd_concurrent_requests    fcr,
       apps.fnd_lookup_values          flv
 WHERE fcr.concurrent_program_id = fcp.concurrent_program_id
   AND trunc(fcr.last_update_date) = trunc(SYSDATE)
   AND flv.lookup_code = fcr.status_code
   AND flv.lookup_type = 'CP_STATUS_CODE'
   AND fcr.phase_code = 'P'
   AND flv.language = 'US'
   AND request_id=143758766
 ORDER BY fcr.request_date desc;

col GROUP_NAME for a35
SELECT
name group_name
, sector_size sector_size
, block_size block_size
, allocation_unit_size allocation_unit_size
, state state
, type type
, round(total_mb/1024,2) total_gb
, round((total_mb - free_mb)/1024,2) used_gb
,round(free_mb/1024,2) free_gb
, ROUND((1- (free_mb / total_mb))*100, 2) pct_used
FROM
v$asm_diskgroup
where name like '%FNRP2%'
ORDER BY
name
;

col program for a10

select to_char(sysdate,'hh24:mi'), username, program , a.sid, a.serial#, b.name, c.value
from v$session a, v$statname b, v$sesstat c
where 
b.STATISTIC# =c.STATISTIC#
and c.sid=a.sid 
and b.name like 'redo%'
and value>0
order by value;

set pagesize 24 linesize 200 echo off feedback 1 wrap on verify off
column reqid format 9999999999 heading "Request Id"
column sesid format a10 heading "Session"
column ospid format a10 heading "OS Pid"
column USER_CONCURRENT_PROGRAM_NAME format a45 heading "Program Name"
column user_name format a20 heading "Requestor"
select
   a.request_id reqid,a.status_code,a.phase_code,e.USER_CONCURRENT_PROGRAM_NAME,f.user_name,
   d.sid||','||d.serial# sesid,c.spid ospid
from
   applsys.fnd_concurrent_requests a,
   applsys.fnd_concurrent_processes b,
   v$process c, v$session d,
   apps.fnd_concurrent_programs_tl e,
   apps.fnd_user f
where
   a.controlling_manager=b.concurrent_process_id
   and c.spid=a.oracle_process_id
   and c.addr=d.paddr
   and e.concurrent_program_id=a.concurrent_program_id
   and a.requested_by = f.user_id
   and d.sid=nvl('&Sid',999999)
   --and a.phase_code='R'
   and b.instance_number=(select instance_number from v$instance)
   and e.language=USERENV('LANG');

-dbc-prd2-vm-3075

select
--	vt.xidusn,
--	vt.xidslot,
--	vt.xidsqn,
	vs.sid,
	vs.serial#,
	vs.inst_id,
	vs.status,
	vs.username,
	vs.program,
	vs.machine,
--	vt.used_ublk,
	vt.start_time,
	TO_CHAR(SYSDATE, 'MM-DD-YYYY HH24:MI:SS') Current_Time
from gv$transaction vt, gv$session vs
where vt.addr = vs.taddr
order by vt.start_time;

select * from gv$session where sid=1352 and serial#=42135;

SELECT 
    s.username,
    SUM(ss.value)/1024/1024/1024 AS redo_size_gb
FROM 
    v$session s
JOIN 
    v$sesstat ss
    ON s.sid = ss.sid
JOIN 
    v$statname sn
    ON ss.statistic# = sn.statistic#
WHERE 
    sn.name = 'redo size'  -- This statistic captures the amount of redo generated
AND 
    s.username IS NOT NULL  -- Exclude background processes
GROUP BY 
    s.username
ORDER BY 
    redo_size_gb DESC;


set lines 300
col USERNAME for a15
SELECT s.sid, s.serial#, s.username, s.program,
i.block_changes
FROM gv$session s, gv$sess_io i
WHERE s.sid = i.sid
ORDER BY 5 desc
;




set lines 300
col USERNAME for a15
SELECT s.sid, s.serial#, s.username, s.program,
t.used_ublk, t.used_urec
FROM gv$session s, gv$transaction t
WHERE s.taddr = t.addr
ORDER BY 5 desc, 6 desc
;





set lines 200
set pages 100
set verify off
col username format a20
col program format a30
col module format a30
select s.sid,s.serial#,s.module,s.username,s.program,to_char(s.logon_time,'DD-MON-YY HH24:MI:SS') "Logon Time",round(a.value/1024/1024,2)||' M' "Redo in MB"
from gv$session s, gv$sesstat a, gv$statname b
where a.statistic# = b.statistic#
and name='redo size'
and s.sid = a.sid
and round(a.value/1024/1024,2)>nvl('&redo_size_in_MB',0)
order by a.value desc
;

2.App team reporte that they are receiving the following error while validating:
ORA-01502: index PLT_ADMIN.WKF_COLLECTED_MESSAGE_PK or partition of such index is in unusable state
3.DBA team is checking on it.
4.DBA team suggested app team to rebuild the index from the tool.
5.App team is unable to get the approval for rebuilding the index.
6.DBA team is checking for the alternatives to create the index from backend
7.DBA team found that one DBMS scheduler job is active in the backend which rebuilds the index WKF_COLLECTED_MESSAGE_PK.
8.Sessions from ANF_APPL schema was blocking the scheduler job.
9.DBA team informed app team has to check on the blocking session so that the dbms job can rebuild the index.
10.SRE team ramped down the services PTEEDC, PTEODC, PTESDC , GOPHER in all 3 DC(s) on all the three regions to clear all the session which are accessing the WKF_COLLECTED_MESSAGE table.
11.DBA team killed the last blocking sessions to continue index rebuild.
12.After clearing all the blocking session the DBMS SCHEDULER job completed fine and the index status became Valid.
13.APP and SRE teams validated from their end and confirmed that no issues observed after this.
14.Network-DevOps-DC Team Confirmed successful implementation of CHG1873354.

select al.name
from gv$log_history lh, gv$archived_log al
where lh.recid >=
(select min(recid)-4 from gv$log_history where first_change# <=
(select min(change#) from gv$recover_file)
and next_change# >=
(select min(change#) from gv$recover_file))
and lh.first_change# = al.first_change#
and lh.thread# = al.thread#
and al.standby_dest = 'NO';

SELECT
name group_name
, sum(round(total_mb/1024,2)) total_gb
, sum(round((total_mb - free_mb)/1024,2)) used_gb
,sum(round(free_mb/1024,2)) free_gb
FROM
v$asm_diskgroup
where name like '%DG_DWHPRD_DT%'
group by name
;

* If we receive any repeated alert on the dashboard related to the high memory usage in the host, Please check the splunk process.

### How to check 
1. Login to the host
2. Run the command: 

```sh
pids=$(pgrep -d, -x splunkd)
if [ -n "$pids" ]; then
  top -b -n 1 -p "$pids"
else
  echo "splunkd: PROCESS IS NOT RUNNING"
fi
```
* If splunk is already down then ignore the next steps.
* If the %MEM of the splunk process is high (for example in case of lnxdb-prd2-vm-904 or lnxdb-prd2-vm-905 it was more than 20%), then inform in the gc "High memory utilization by splunk process" and stop the splunk process

### How to stop

* Get the DACT and login as oracle user
* Check the memory usage of the host
free -g
* Check status of the process. It should show that process is running.
/oracle/export/Splunk/splunkforwarder/bin/splunk status
* Stop the process
/oracle/export/Splunk/splunkforwarder/bin/splunk stop
* Check the status again.It should show that process is NOT running.
/oracle/export/Splunk/splunkforwarder/bin/splunk status
* Check the host level memory usage again. Free memory will be higher than before. 
free -g

set linesize 100 pages 100 trimspool on numwidth 14 
col name format a25
col owner format a15 
col "Used (GB)" format a15
col "Free (GB)" format a15 
col "(Used) %" format a15 
col "Size (M)" format a15 
SELECT 
 d.status "Status", 
 d.tablespace_name "Name", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(a.bytes / 1024 / 1024 /1024, 0),'99,999,990.90') "Size (GB)", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(a.bytes - NVL(f.bytes, 0), 0)/1024/1024 /1024,'99999999.99') "Used (GB)", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(f.bytes / 1024 / 1024 /1024, 0),'99,999,990.90') "Free (GB)", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL((a.bytes - NVL(f.bytes, 0)) / a.bytes * 100, 0), '990.00') "(Used) %"
 FROM sys.dba_tablespaces d, 
 (select tablespace_name, sum(bytes) bytes from dba_data_files group by tablespace_name) a, 
 (select tablespace_name, sum(bytes) bytes from dba_free_space group by tablespace_name) f WHERE 
 d.tablespace_name = a.tablespace_name(+) AND d.tablespace_name = f.tablespace_name(+) AND NOT 
 (d.extent_management like 'LOCAL' AND d.contents like 'TEMPORARY') 
UNION ALL 
SELECT 
 d.status "Status", 
 d.tablespace_name "Name", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(a.bytes / 1024 / 1024 /1024, 0),'99,999,990.90') "Size (GB)", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(t.bytes,0)/1024/1024 /1024,'99999999.99') "Used (GB)",
 TO_CHAR(NVL((a.bytes -NVL(t.bytes, 0)) / 1024 / 1024 /1024, 0),'99,999,990.90') "Free (GB)", 
 TO_CHAR(NVL(t.bytes / a.bytes * 100, 0), '990.00') "(Used) %" 
 FROM sys.dba_tablespaces d, 
 (select tablespace_name, sum(bytes) bytes from dba_temp_files group by tablespace_name) a, 
 (select tablespace_name, sum(bytes_cached) bytes from v$temp_extent_pool group by tablespace_name) t 
 WHERE d.tablespace_name = a.tablespace_name(+) AND d.tablespace_name = t.tablespace_name(+) AND 
 d.extent_management like 'LOCAL' AND d.contents like 'TEMPORARY'
 order by 2;

1. Duty has been engaged EOC-INC10650436-EM-Allen1 Linux host dbc-prd2-2109 experienced an unexpected reboot on 23 jan 07:59 PT
2. Priot to this event Duty received agent unreachable alert for 9th node of CSFPRD primary database (dbc-prd2-2109).
3. Hosting team has been involved via INC10650344 to investigate.
4. Host has rebooted and DB services came up. Duty ran APPV and DR DB post which DB and ERP services have been validated and found running as expected.
5. Hosting team have an existing TAC case : 700315205 rcdn9-fab1-ucs01-174 || dbc-prd1-2109 || 2/3 || Need RCA for reboot
7. Duty raised jira DEJS-108368 for RCA and SR#4-0001869965 - CSFPRD : dbc-prd2-2109 : Host reboot issue .
8. Currently hosting team is checking with Red Hat(RH case #04343502) to investigate the root cause of the issue (ETA 2 hr)
9. Hosting team has suggested to clear the cache on the CSFPRD active and passive DB nodes .
10. DBA is awaiting further inputs from red hat and Oracle for their next steps related to parameter fs.dentry-fs-klimit kernel parameter update , to limit the number of negative dentries and thus reduce contention on the spin locks.
11. Currently, the DBA and hosting teams are collaborating with Oracle and Red Hat engineers on the call.
12. High Dentry value is detected on multiple nodes in the CSFPRD DB, host got rebooted with soft lock CPU error.
13. Below steps are completed on the TS1CSF nodes (dbc-pts1-2116 to dbc-pts1-2125) to test before implementing on prod.

STEP 1: One time clear cache : echo 2 > /proc/sys/vm/drop_caches
NON-PROD : completed

STEP 2 : Update Parameter dentry-fs-klimit : echo 100 > /proc/sys/fs/dentry-fs-klimit
: echo fs.dentry-fs-klimit = 100>> /etc/sysctl.conf ( update sysctl.conf for permanent update )
: sysctl -p

NON-PROD : completed

14.Based on the observations from TS1CSF , above steps in prod will be implemented post quarter end.
15. As updated, Hosting team have successfully implemented the recommendations suggested by Redhat team in non-production environments. This included a comprehensive cache cleanup and adjusting the dentry FSK limit to 100 to improve the management of negative entries.
16. Performance is currently being monitored in non-production to validate the fix. While production hosts remain stable with no observed issues, the Hosting team will continue to monitor the environment until QE Close. Team will decide on production rollout after QE.

select id,num from(
select id,sum(num) as num,
row_number() over(order by sum(num) desc) as rn from
(
select requester_id as id,count(1) as num from RequestAccepted group by requester_id 
union all
select accepter_id as id,count(1) as num from RequestAccepted group by accepter_id order by 1
)group by id order by 2 desc
)where rn=1

with tab1 as(
select 
salary 
from
(
select id,salary,dense_rank() over(order by salary desc) as rn from employee 
)
where rn=2
)
select
case
when select count(distinct salary) from employee=1 then null
else salary
end as secondhighestsalary 
from tab1

select 
request_at as "day",
round((cancelled_trip/total_trip),2) as "Cancellation Rate"
from
(select 
request_at,
count(*) total_trip,
sum(case when Status='completed' then 1 end) as completed_trip,
coalesce(sum(case when Status like 'cancelled%' then 1 end),0) as cancelled_trip from(
select 
t.id trip_id,
t.client_id userId,
t.driver_id,
t.status,
t.request_at
from trips t join users u on t.client_id=u.users_id 
--or t.driver_id=u.users_id
where u.banned='No' order by t.request_at,t.id
)
group by request_at)





select 
request_at as "day",
round((cancelled_trip/total_trip),2) as "Cancellation Rate"
from
(
select 
	request_at,
	count(*) total_trip,
	sum(case when Status='completed' then 1 end) as completed_trip,
	coalesce(sum(case when Status like 'cancelled%' then 1 end),0) as cancelled_trip 
from(
	select 
		t.id trip_id,
		t.client_id userId,
		t.driver_id,
		t.status,
		t.request_at
	from trips t join users u 
	ON t.client_id=u.users_id /*include clients who are banned*/
    AND u.banned='No'
JOIN Users u
    ON t.driver_id=u.users_id/*include drivers who are banned*/
    AND u.banned='No'
    where t.request_at between to_char('2013-10-01') and to_char('2013-10-03')
	order by t.request_at,t.id)
group by request_at)


1.EOC engaged dba team as they received alert for CI RAOPRD at raoprd-oracle-mvdc.composite
2.CHG2010916 is in progress for RAOPRD.
3.The outage is tagged as NO for the CI.

4.From 15:58 to 17:23 IST, MVDC composite "RAOPRD@raoprd-oracle-mvdc.composite" alerted in zabbixn; however, the application team confirmed that ALLN was operational during this period.
5.The UM team identified there was a sync issue in  MVDC composite as only RCDN synced.
6.Until 18:30 IST (05:00 PT), the MVDC composite showed only one node synced, specifically the RCDN node. Alerts began once the RCDN node went down.
7.The absence of ALLN may be due to a resync event that is not visible clearly; this will be discussed further in the PRB.
8.The reason for Zabbix showing the endpoint as unmonitored is that Grafana retrieves the latest data, which can sometimes take 10 to 15 minutes to update due to ETL processing; this delay is not considered an issue.
9.Both ALLN and RCDN composites were monitored in zabbix correctly , without any issues
10.DBA team brought up the DB services as part of CHG2010916, which cleared the alerts.
11.EOC resolved the case.
12.PRB0093166 has been assigned to UM team.
